                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">عَلِقَ بِهِ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, (S, Mgh, O, Msb, TA,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Ba" lang="ar">عَلَقَ</orth>
                  </form>, (Msb,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">عَلَقٌ</foreign> (S, O, Msb, KL, TA) and <foreign lang="ar">عَلقَةٌ</foreign> (L, TA) [and app. <foreign lang="ar">عُلُوقٌ</foreign> also, as will be seen from what follows]; and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30276-1" target="تعلّق" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n30276"/></foreign>, (S, MA, Mgh, O, Msb,) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30276-2" target="اعتلق" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>; (O, Msb, KL;) <hi rend="ital">It hung to it; it was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, suspended to it:</hi> (so the first and last accord. to the KL, and the second accord. to the MA and common usage: [in the S and Mgh and O, it is merely said that the first and second signify the same:]) [and] <hi rend="ital">it clung, caught, clave, adhered, held,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">stuck fast, to it;</hi> (Msb in explanation of all, and TA * in explanation of the first;) and so   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30276-3" target="تعلّقهُ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n30276"/></foreign>. (S, * O, * TA.) It is said in a prov., (S, O, TA,) asserted in the K to have been mentioned before, which is not found to be the case, (TA,) <quote>
                     <L><foreign lang="ar">عَلِقَتْ <ref cref="n30276-4" target="مَعَالِقَهَا" n="4" type="5" subtype="TFSO" lang="ar"/>وَصَرَّ الجُنْدَبُ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> (S, O, K, [in the CK, erroneously, <foreign lang="ar">مُعالِقَها</foreign>,]) [<hi rend="ital">It</hi> (the bucket, <foreign lang="ar">الدَّلْوُ</foreign>, Z, TA) <hi rend="ital">has become suspended in its places of suspension, and the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">جندب</foreign> (accord. to the S and K a species of locust) <hi rend="ital">has creaked</hi>]: originating from the fact that a man went to a well, and suspended his well-rope to the rope thereof, and then went to the owner of the well, and claimed to be his neighbour [and therefore to have a right to the use of the well]; but the owner refused his assent, and ordered him to depart; whereupon he uttered these words, meaning The heat has come, [see <foreign lang="ar">صَرَّ الجُنْدَبُ</foreign> in art. <foreign lang="ar">جدب</foreign>,] and I am not able to depart. (S, O. [See more in Freytag's Arab. Prov. ii. 91.]) And one says, <foreign lang="ar">عَلِقَ الشَّوْكُ بِالثَّوْبِ</foreign>, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Ba" lang="ar">عَلَقَ</orth>
                  </form>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">عَلَقٌ</foreign>; and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30276-5" target="تعلّق" n="5" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar" select="n30276"/>بِهِ</foreign>; meaning <hi rend="ital">The thorns clung, caught,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">to the garment.</hi> (Msb.) And <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30276-6" target="اعتلق" n="6" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>ظُفْرِى بِالشَّىْءِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">My nail clung, caught,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">to the thing.</hi> (Msb.) And <foreign lang="ar">عَلِقَ الظَّبْىُ فِى الحِبَالَةِ</foreign>, (S, O,) or <foreign lang="ar">الصَّيْدُ</foreign>; (K;) or <foreign lang="ar">عَلِقَ الوَحْشُ بِٱلْحِبَالَةِ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">عُلُوقٌ</foreign>, (Msb,) [<hi rend="ital">The gazelle,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the animal of the chase, became caught,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">stuck fast, in the snare;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the wild animal became caught,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">held fast, thereby,</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">became withheld from getting loose</hi> [<hi rend="ital">thereby</hi>]: whence the saying, <foreign lang="ar">عَلِقَ الخَصْمُ بِخَصْمِهِ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30276-7" target="تعلّق" n="7" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar" select="n30276"/>بِهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The antagonist became held fast,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">withheld from getting loose, by his antagonist;</hi> and also <hi rend="ital">the antagonist clung,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">held fast, to his antagonist</hi>]. (Msb.) [         <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  The primary significations are those mentioned above in the first sentence: and hence several other significations here following.          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">عَلِقَ عَلَى كَذَا</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30276-8" target="تعلّق" n="8" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar" select="n30276"/>عَلَيْهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">It depended upon such a thing, as a condition.</hi>          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">عَلِقَ بِهِ</foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30276-9" target="تعلّق" n="9" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n30276"/></foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">It pertained to him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it: it concerned him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it.</hi> And <hi rend="ital">He had a hold upon it: he had a concern in it.</hi>]          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">عَلِقَهَا</foreign>, (S, O,) or <foreign lang="ar">عَلِقَهُ</foreign>, (K,) and <foreign lang="ar">عَلِقَ بِهَا</foreign>, (S, O,) or <foreign lang="ar">بِهِ</foreign>, (K,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">عُلُوقٌ</foreign> (S, O, K) and <foreign lang="ar">عَلَقٌ</foreign> (K [and mentioned also in the S and O but app. as a simple subst.]) and <foreign lang="ar">عِلْقٌ</foreign> [but see this below voce <foreign lang="ar">عَلَقٌ</foreign>] and <foreign lang="ar">عَلَاقَةٌ</foreign>, (K,) [<hi rend="ital">He became attached by love to her,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">to him;</hi>] <hi rend="ital">he loved</hi> (S, O, K) <hi rend="ital">her,</hi> (S, O,) or <hi rend="ital">him;</hi> (K;) and so <foreign lang="ar">عَلِقَ حُبُّهَا بِقَلْبِهِ</foreign>; (S, O;) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30276-10" target="تعلّقها" n="10" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n30276"/></foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">تعلّق بِهَا</foreign>; [the former of these two phrases being used for the latter, agreeably with a saying of IAmb cited in the TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">ارى</foreign>, that <foreign lang="ar">تَعَلَّقْتُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">فُلَانًا</foreign> is for <foreign lang="ar">تعلّقت بِفُلَانٍ</foreign>;] like   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30276-11" target="اعتلق" n="11" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> [i. e. <foreign lang="ar">اعتلقها</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">اعتلق بها</foreign>], (K,) or <foreign lang="ar">اعتلقهُ</foreign>, (S,) or <foreign lang="ar">اعتلق بِهِ</foreign>; (TA;) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30276-12" target="عُلِّقَهَا" n="12" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, (S, * O, * K, TA,) from <foreign lang="ar">عَلَاقَةُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الحُبِّ</foreign>, (S, O, TA,) and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30276-13" target="عُلِّقَ" n="13" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>بِهَا</foreign>, (TA,) [but this last verb is more commonly trans. by itself, for ex.,] El-Aashà says, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">عُلِّقْتُهَا عَرَضًا وَعُلِّقَتْ رَجُلًا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">غَيْرِى وَعُلِّقَ أُخْرَى غَيْرَهَا الرَّجُلُ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">I became attached to her accidentally, and she became attached to a man other than me, and the man became attached to another female, other than her</hi>]. (S, O. [See also another ex., in a verse of 'Antarah, cited voce <foreign lang="ar">زَعَمَ</foreign>.]) [See also <foreign lang="ar">عَلَقٌ</foreign>, below.]          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>    
      <foreign lang="ar">عَلِقَتْ مِنْهُ كُلَّ <ref cref="n30276-14" target="مَعْلَقٍ" n="14" type="1" subtype="SO" lang="ar"/></foreign> [which may be rendered <hi rend="ital">She captivated him wholly</hi>] occurs in a trad. as [virtually] meaning <hi rend="ital">he loved her, and was vehemently desirous of her.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="7">-b7-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">عَلِقَتْ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">نَفْسُهُ الشَّىْءَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">His soul,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">mind, clung to the thing persistently.</hi> (L, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="8">-b8-</sense>    
      <foreign lang="ar">قَدْ عَلِقَ الكِبَرُ <ref cref="n30276-15" target="مَعَالِقَهُ" n="15" type="1" subtype="SO" lang="ar"/></foreign> [app. meaning <hi rend="ital">Old age has taken hold in its holding places,</hi> or, agreeably with what is said in the <pb n="2133"/> next sentence, <hi rend="ital">has had its effects</hi>], in which <foreign lang="ar">معالق</foreign> is pl. of <foreign lang="ar">مَعْلَقٌ</foreign>, is said to an old man. (TA.) And of everything that has had its effect [so I here render <foreign lang="ar">وَقَعَ مَوْقِعَهُ</foreign>, but see art. <foreign lang="ar">وقع</foreign>], one says, <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30276-16" target="مَعَالِقَهُ" n="16" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>عَلِقَ</foreign>. (TA, and Ham p. 172.)          <sense type="b" n="9">-b9-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">عَلِقَتْ مَرَاسِيهَا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بِذِى رَمْرَامٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Their anchors have clung to a place having the species of herbage called</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">رمرام</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">they are abiding therein,</hi> (see <foreign lang="ar">مِرْسَاةٌ</foreign>, in art. <foreign lang="ar">رسو</foreign>,)] is said of camels when they are at rest, or at ease, and their eyes are refreshed by the pasturage; and is a prov., applied to persons in the like condition by reason of their means of subsistence. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="10">-b10-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">عَلِقَ بِهِ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">عَلَقٌ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">He contended with him in an altercation</hi> [as though clinging to him]; <hi rend="ital">disputed with him;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">litigated with him.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="11">-b11-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">لَا يَعْلَقُ بِكَ</foreign> means <foreign lang="ar">لا يَلِيقُ بك</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">It will not be suitable to thee; it will not befit thee</hi>]. (S and K in art. <foreign lang="ar">ليق</foreign>.)          <sense type="b" n="12">-b12-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">عَلِقَ يَفْعَلُ كَذَا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He set about, began,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">betook himself to, doing such a thing.</hi> (S, O, K.) <foreign lang="ar">فَعَلِقُوا وَجْهَهُ ضَرْبًا</foreign> occurs in a trad., meaning <hi rend="ital">They set about,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">betook themselves to, smiting his face.</hi> (TA.) And a rájiz says, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">عَلِقَ حَوْضِى نُغَرٌ مُكِبُّ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">Nughar</hi> (a species of birds) <hi rend="ital">bending down their heads</hi>] <hi rend="ital">betook themselves to coming for the purpose of drinking to my</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">حوض</foreign> [or <hi rend="ital">watering-trough</hi>]: or, as some say, <hi rend="ital">liked it, and frequented it.</hi> (S, O.)          <sense type="b" n="13">-b13-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">مَا عَلِقْتُ أَقْولُهُ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">I did not cease saying it;</hi> like <foreign lang="ar">ما نَشِبْتُ</foreign>. (A in art. <foreign lang="ar">نشب</foreign>.) [Thus <foreign lang="ar">عَلِقَ</foreign> has two contr. meanings.]          <sense type="b" n="14">-b14-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">عَلِقَتِ الإِبِلُ</foreign>

                  </form>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">عُلُوقٌ</foreign>, means <hi rend="ital">they reached and took with their mouths.</hi> (TA.) Hence, (TA,) it is said in a trad., <foreign lang="ar">أَرْوَاحُ الشُّهَدَآءِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">فِى حَوَاصِلِ طَيْرٍ خُضْرٍ تَعْلُقُ مِنْ وَرَقِ الجَنَّةِ</foreign>, (S, Msb, *) or <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ ثِمَارِ الجَنَّةِ</foreign>, (TA,) and, as some relate it, <foreign lang="ar">تَعْلَقُ</foreign>, (Msb, TA,) [both as meaning <hi rend="ital">The souls of the martyrs are in the crops of green birds that eat of the leaves,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">fruits, of Paradise,</hi>] but the former relation is that which should be followed, because the latter requires that one should say <foreign lang="ar">فِى ورق الجنّة</foreign> [or <foreign lang="ar">فى ثمار الجنّة</foreign>], though the latter is said to be the more common. (Msb.) One says also, <foreign lang="ar">عَلِقَتِ الإِبِلُ</foreign>, aor.

                  <hi rend="ital">He knew his affair.</hi> (K.)          <sense type="b" n="17">-b17-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">عَلِقَتِ المَرْأَةُ</foreign>, (S, Mgh, O, K,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">عُلُوقٌ</foreign>, (Mgh,) or <foreign lang="ar">عَلَقٌ</foreign>, (TA,) <hi rend="ital">The woman conceived,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became pregnant.</hi> (S, Mgh, O, K.) Hence the saying, <foreign lang="ar">الغِرَاسُ تَبَدَّلُ بِالعُلُوقِ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">The set,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">shoot that is planted, becomes changed by pullulating</hi>]; a metaphorical phrase; meaning that what is planted becomes changed because it increases and rises when it clings to the earth and germinates. (Mgh.)          <sense type="b" n="18">-b18-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">عَلِقَتِ الدَّابَّةُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The beast drank water and the leech</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">العَلَقَةُ</foreign>) <hi rend="ital">clave to it:</hi> (S, O, K:) or, accord. to an explanation of [the part. n.] <foreign lang="ar">مَعْلُوقٌ</foreign> by Lth, one says <foreign lang="ar">عُلِقَت</foreign>, of the form of that whereof the agent is not named, meaning <hi rend="ital">it had leeches</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">عَلَق</foreign>) <hi rend="ital">that had taken hold upon its fauces when it drank:</hi> (O:) or <foreign lang="ar">عُلِقَ</foreign>, also, like <foreign lang="ar">عُنِىَ</foreign>, is used in this sense, (K, * TA,) said of a man and of a beast.                      <itype>2</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">علّقهُ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, (S, O, Msb, K,) i. e. <foreign lang="ar">الشَّىْءَ</foreign>, (S, O, Msb,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">تَعْلِيقٌ</foreign>; (S, O, K;) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30277-1" target="اعلقهُ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, (S, * O, * Msb,) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30277-2" target="تعلّقهُ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n30276"/></foreign>; (S, O, K;) signify the same. (S, O, Msb, K.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">علّق الشَّىْءَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بِالشَّىْءِ</foreign>, (Mgh, Msb, K,) inf. n. as above, <hi rend="ital">He hung,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">suspended, the thing to the thing;</hi> and so <foreign lang="ar">مِنَ الشَّىْءِ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْهِ</foreign>: (TA:) [and] <hi rend="ital">he made the thing to cling, catch, cleave, adhere, hold,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">stick fast, to the thing;</hi> as also <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30277-3" target="اعلقهُ" n="3" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>بِهِ</foreign>. (Msb.) [For ex.,] one says, <foreign lang="ar">عَلَّقْتُ رِشَائِى بِرِشَائِكَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I have suspended my well-rope to thy well-rope</hi>]: and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30277-4" target="أَعْلَقَ" n="4" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar" select="n30277-3"/>رِشَآءَهُ بِرِشَآءِ البِئْرِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He suspended his well-rope to the rope of the well</hi>]. (S, O.) [See also an ex. of the latter verb in a verse cited voce <foreign lang="ar">رَافِضٌ</foreign>.] And <foreign lang="ar">علّقهُ عَلَى الوَتِدِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He hung it on the peg</hi>]: and in like manner, <foreign lang="ar">علّق الشَّىْءَ خَلْفَهُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He hung the thing behind him</hi>]; as, for instance, a <foreign lang="ar">حَقِيبَة</foreign>, &amp;c., behind the camel's saddle. (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30277-5" target="تعلّق" n="5" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar" select="n30276"/>مَعَاذَةً</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He hung</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">عَلَّقَ</foreign>) <hi rend="ital">upon himself an amulet.</hi> (S, O.) And <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30277-6" target="اعلق" n="6" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>بِالغَرْبِ بَعِيرَيْنِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He coupled two camels to the end of the well-rope</hi> [<hi rend="ital">to the other end of which was attached the large bucket</hi>]. (IF, K.) [And in like manner they say in the present day, <foreign lang="ar">علّق الخَيْلَ فِى العَرَبَةِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He harnessed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">attached, the horses to the carriage.</hi>] And <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30277-7" target="اعلق" n="7" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>أَظْفَارَهُ فِى الشَّىْءِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He made his nails to cling, catch,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">cleave, to the thing.</hi> (S, TA.) And [in like manner,] <foreign lang="ar">علّق يَدَهُ</foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30277-8" target="اعلقها" n="8" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He made his hands to cling,</hi> &amp;c.], followed by <foreign lang="ar">فى</foreign> before the object: both signify the same. (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">علّق الدَّابَّةَ</foreign>, meaning <foreign lang="ar">علّق عَلَيْهَا</foreign> [for <foreign lang="ar">علّق عليها</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">المِخْلَاةَ</foreign>, agreeably with modern usage, i. e. <hi rend="ital">He hung upon the beast the nose-bag</hi> containing barley, or the like; or <hi rend="ital">he supplied the beast with</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَلِيق</foreign>, which means <hi rend="ital">barley,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the like, that is hung upon the beast</hi>]. (TA.) [And hence, as is indicated in the T and TA, <foreign lang="ar">علّق</foreign> signifies, by a metaphor, <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">He supplied with</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَلِيق</foreign> as meaning <hi rend="ital">wine.</hi>] And <foreign lang="ar">علّق رَاحِلَتَهُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He loosed the halter,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">leading-rope, from the muzzle of his riding-camel and threw it</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">hung it</hi>] <hi rend="ital">upon her shoulders, to give her ease.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [The primary significations are those mentioned in the second sentence of this paragraph: and hence several other significations here following.          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">علّقهُ بِكَذَا</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى كَذَا</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">He made it to depend upon such a thing, as a condition.</hi>] You say, <foreign lang="ar">عَلَّقْتُ عِتْقَ عَبْدِى بِمَوْتِى</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I made the freedom of my slave to depend upon my death</hi>]. (TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">دبر</foreign>.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">إِنْ أَنْطِقْ أُطَلَّقْ وَإِنْ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَسْكُتْ أُعَلَّقْ</foreign>, in the story of Umm-Zara, means [<hi rend="ital">If I speak, I am divorced; and if I be silent, I am left in suspense,</hi> i. e.,] he leaves me like that which is suspended, (O, TA,) neither retained nor divorced. (TA.) [And similar to this is the phrase <foreign lang="ar">تَعْلِيقُ أَفْعَالِ القُلُوبِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The suspending of the verbs significant of operations of the mind from government, as to the letter but not as to the meaning:</hi>] see <foreign lang="ar">مُعَلَّقٌ</foreign>.          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  [<foreign lang="ar">علّق البِنَآءَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He made the building,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">structure, pensile,</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">supported above the ground,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">above a stage</hi> or <hi rend="ital">floor, by pillars</hi> or <hi rend="ital">piers</hi> or <hi rend="ital">otherwise.</hi> Hence,] the saying <foreign lang="ar">نَقَبُوا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الحَائِطَ وَعَلَّقُوهُ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">They dug beneath the wall</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">made a hole through it</hi>] <hi rend="ital">and left it</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">rendered it</hi>] <foreign lang="ar">مُعَلَّقًا</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">pensile,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">supported above the ground,</hi> being partially hollowed beneath]. (Mgh.)          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  [<foreign lang="ar">علّق فِى حَاشِيَةِ كِتَابٍ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He appended a note in the margin of a book</hi> or <hi rend="ital">writing.</hi>]          <sense type="b" n="7">-b7-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">علّق بَابًا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He set up, and fixed, a door,</hi> (Mgh, TA,) <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى دَارِهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">upon,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">to, his house</hi>]. (Mgh.)          <sense type="b" n="8">-b8-</sense>  And (TA) <hi rend="ital">He closed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">made fast, a door, with a kind of latch,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">sliding bolt;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">أَزْلَجَهُ</foreign>, (O, TA,) or <foreign lang="ar">أَرْتَجَهُ</foreign>; (K;) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30277-9" target="اعلقهُ" n="9" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>. (TA.) [See <foreign lang="ar">مِعْلَاقٌ</foreign>.]          <sense type="b" n="9">-b9-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">عُلِّقَهَا</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">عُلِّقَ بِهَا</foreign>, in which the pronoun denoting the object relates to a woman: see 1, former half.          <sense type="b" n="10">-b10-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">عَلَّقَ فُلَانٌ دَمَ فُلَانٍ</foreign> [app. meaning <hi rend="ital">Such a one attached to himself responsibility for the blood of such a one</hi>] is said when the former is the slayer of the latter. (TA. [Thus I find the phrase there written: but perhaps the right reading is <foreign lang="ar">عُلِّقَ</foreign>.])          <sense type="b" n="11">-b11-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">عَلَّقَهُ</foreign> also signifies <hi rend="ital">He joined him,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">overtook him.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="12">-b12-</sense>  And <hi rend="ital">He learned it,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">took it</hi> or <hi rend="ital">received it</hi> [from another]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="13">-b13-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">عَلِّقُوا رَمَقَهُ بِشَىْءٍ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Give ye to him something that shall stay,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">arrest, what remains in him of life.</hi> (Z, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="14">-b14-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">عَلَّقْتُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مَعَ فُلَانٍ عَلِيقَةً</foreign>, (S, TA,) and <foreign lang="ar">مَعَ القَوْمِ</foreign>, (TA,) <hi rend="ital">I sent with such a one,</hi> (S, TA,) and <hi rend="ital">with the people,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">party,</hi> (TA,) <hi rend="ital">a camel for the purpose of bringing corn for me upon it.</hi> (S, TA. [See <foreign lang="ar">عَلِيقَةٌ</foreign>.]) <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">اِرْضَ مِنَ المَرْكَبِ بِالتَّعْلِيقِ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> 
                  <pb n="2134"/> is a prov., said to a man who is thereby enjoined to be content with a part of that which he wants, instead of the whole thereof; like him who rides the camel termed <foreign lang="ar">عَلِيقَة</foreign> one time after another time: [so that it means <hi rend="ital">Be thou content, instead of the riding</hi> constantly, or <hi rend="ital">instead of the beast that is ridden</hi> only, <hi rend="ital">with the sending a camel to bring corn,</hi> upon which thou mayest ride occasionally:] (TA:) or the meaning may be, <hi rend="ital">be thou content, instead of</hi> thy <hi rend="ital">riding, with the hanging</hi> of thy goods upon the beast: or the meaning may be, <hi rend="ital">be thou content, in respect of the beast that is ridden, with the hanging</hi> [thy goods] upon him in thy turn.                      <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">عَلَاقَةٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> [is originally an inf. n.: and as a simple subst. signifies <hi rend="ital">An attachment, a tie,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a connection;</hi> as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30295-1" target="عُلْقَةٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n30284"/></foreign>, mentioned in the TA, in art. <foreign lang="ar">ربط</foreign>, together with <foreign lang="ar">وُصْلَةٌ</foreign>, as syn. with <foreign lang="ar">رَابِطَةٌ</foreign>:] a word relating to things conceived in the mind; as love, and contention in an altercation:   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30295-2" target="عِلَاقَةٌ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n30296"/></foreign> relating to things extrinsic to the mind; as a bow, and a whip: (Kull p. 262:) see <foreign lang="ar">عَلَقٌ</foreign>, last quarter.          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [Hence, as denoting an attachment, or a tie,] <hi rend="ital">Love,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">friendship;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">such as is true,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">sincere;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">حُبٌّ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">صَدَاقَةٌ</foreign>: (K, TA:) [or as expl. voce <foreign lang="ar">عَلَقٌ</foreign>, last quarter:] or it means <foreign lang="ar">عَلَاقَةُ حُبٍّ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">an attachment,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a tie,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a clinging, of love</hi>]: (S, O:) Lh mentions, on the authority of Ks, and as known to As, the saying <foreign lang="ar">لَهَا فِى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">قَلْبِى عَلَاقَةُ حُبٍّ</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">There is to her, in my heart, an attachment,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a tie,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a clinging, of love</hi>]; and likewise, on the authority of the former, but as unknown to As, <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30295-3" target="عِلْقُ" n="3" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>حُبٍّ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30295-4" target="عِلَاقَةُ" n="4" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>حُبٍّ</foreign>, though As knew the phrase <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30295-5" target="عَلَقُ" n="5" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>حُبٍّ</foreign>: (TA:) or <foreign lang="ar">عَلَاقَةُ حُبٍّ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">love to which one clings.</hi> (Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  And <hi rend="ital">A contention in an altercation; a dispute;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a litigation:</hi> (K: [see also <foreign lang="ar">عَلَقٌ</foreign>, near the end of the paragraph:]) or it means <foreign lang="ar">عَلَاقَةُ خُصُومَةٍ</foreign> [app. one's <hi rend="ital">connection in such a contention</hi>]: (S, O:) or <foreign lang="ar">عَلَاقَةُ خُصُومَةٍ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">the proportion</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">share</hi>] <hi rend="ital">that one holds</hi> [<hi rend="ital">in such a contention;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">what pertains to one thereof;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">one's concern therein</hi>]: (Msb:) [for]          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">عَلَاقَةٌ</foreign> also signifies <hi rend="ital">A thing upon which one has,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">retains, a hold;</hi> like   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30295-6" target="عُلْقَةٌ" n="6" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n30284"/></foreign> in the saying <foreign lang="ar">كُلُّ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بَيْعٍ أَبْقَى عُلْقَةً فَهُوَ بِاطِلٌ</foreign> i. e. [<hi rend="ital">Every sale that leaves remaining</hi>] <hi rend="ital">a thing upon which the seller retains a hold</hi> [<hi rend="ital">is null</hi>]. (Msb.) [<hi rend="ital">There is not to his door</hi>] <hi rend="ital">a thing that is opened with a key nor</hi> [<hi rend="ital">a thing that is opened</hi>] <hi rend="ital">without it.</hi> (A, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">مِعْلَاقٌ</foreign> also signifies The <hi rend="ital">tongue</hi> (O, K) of a man: (O:) or <hi rend="ital">an eloquent tongue.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">رَجُلٌ ذُو مِعْلَاقٍ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">A man whose antagonist, when he clings to him, will not</hi> [<hi rend="ital">be able to</hi>] <hi rend="ital">free himself from him:</hi> (Mbr, Z, TA:) or <hi rend="ital">a man vehement in altercation</hi> or <hi rend="ital">dispute</hi> or <hi rend="ital">litigation,</hi> (IDrd, S, O, K,) <hi rend="ital">who clings to arguments,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">pleas,</hi> (IDrd, O, K,) <hi rend="ital">and supplies them;</hi> (IDrd, O;) and <foreign lang="ar">رَجُلٌ مِعْلَاقٌ</foreign> signifies the same.
